Now I also need to make sure the CUDA source file has a proper `extern "C"` launcher that can be called via ctypes. Let me also check that the `inter_chunk_kernel_launcher` symbol is exported from the .so file. But there might be an issue with the ctypes approach: the CUDA kernel launch (`<<<BH, 128>>>`) is asynchronous, and when called from a non-CUDA-aware host thread, it might not work correctly. ctypes calls run in the Python thread, not a CUDA stream. Actually, CUDA kernel launches work fine from any host thread as long as the CUDA runtime is initialized (which PyTorch handles). The `<<<>>>` syntax internally calls `cudaLaunchKernel`. But there's a subtlety: the ctypes call might not properly set up the CUDA context. PyTorch sets up the CUDA context on the main thread. When we call through ctypes, the CUDA runtime should use the current context. … +1 more lines

assistant
Let me provide a summary of what was done and the results.
assistant

Summary

The implementation is in solution.py and passes python check.py across all 4 shapes (PASS).

Approach

Intra-chunk: Uses batched cuBLAS operations (torch.bmm + torch.linalg.solve_triangular) which are efficient for the large batch sizes (B×H×NT up to 512).

Inter-chunk recurrence: Uses these optimizations:

  • Pre-computes all-chunk Aqk in a single batched bmm call
  • Fuses w@S and q@S into one stacked bmm per chunk
  • Uses torch.compile(mode="max-autotune") on the inter-chunk loop, which generates autotuned Triton kernels for the per-chunk matmuls

Performance

| Shape | Time | Peak Fraction | |-------|------|---------------| | B=2, T=1024, H=8 | 0.44ms | 0.0099 | | B=2, T=2048, H=8 | 0.96ms | 0.0090 | | B=1, T=4096, H=8 | 1.31ms | 0.0066 | | B=1, T=2048, H=4 | 0.52ms | 0.0042 | | Geomean | | 0.0070 |

Gap Analysis

The 0.0070 peak fraction is below the 0.1 target. The bottleneck is the inter-chunk recurrence loop — the sequential dependency on state S prevents parallelization across chunks, and the small matmul sizes (batch=16, M=64, K/V=128) mean launch overhead dominates over compute.

Closing the remaining ~14x gap requires a fully hand-tuned CUDA kernel using warp-group Tensor Core MMA instructions (nvcuda::wmma or mma.sync on SM120). I attempted this approach but ran into persistent pybind11 binding issues with torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline. The correct approach would be to write a standalone .cu file that uses warp-group cooperative matrix multiply with bf16 inputs and fp32 accumulation, keeping state S in shared memory, and processing all chunks for one (B,H) pair in a single block.

## Summary The implementation is in `solution.py` and passes `python check.py` across all 4 shapes (PASS). ### Approach **Intra-chunk:** Uses batched cuBLAS operations (`torch.bmm` + `torch.linalg.solve_triangular`) which are efficient for the large batch sizes (B×H×NT up to 512). **Inter-chunk recurrence:** Uses these optimizations: - Pre-computes all-chunk Aqk in a single batched `bmm` call - Fuses `w@S` and `q@S` into one stacked `bmm` per chunk - Uses `torch.compile(mode="max-autotune")` on the inter-chunk loop, which generates autotuned Triton kernels for the per-chunk matmuls ### Performance | Shape | Time | Peak Fraction | |-------|------|---------------| | B=2, T=1024, H=8 | 0.44ms | 0.0099 | | B=2, T=2048, H=8 | 0.96ms | 0.0090 | | B=1, T=4096, H=8 | 1.31ms | 0.0066 | | B=1, T=2048, H=4 | 0.52ms | 0.0042 | | **Geomean** | | **0.0070** | ### Gap Analysis The 0.0070 peak fraction is below the 0.1 target. The bottleneck is the inter-chunk recurrence loop — the sequential dependency on state S prevents parallelization across chunks, and the small matmul sizes (batch=16, M=64, K/V=128) mean launch overhead dominates over compute. Closing the remaining ~14x gap requires a fully hand-tuned CUDA kernel using warp-group Tensor Core MMA instructions (`nvcuda::wmma` or `mma.sync` on SM120). I attempted this approach but ran into persistent pybind11 binding issues with `torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline`. The correct approach would be to write a standalone `.cu` file that uses warp-group cooperative matrix multiply with bf16 inputs and fp32 accumulation, keeping state S in shared memory, and processing all chunks for one (B,H) pair in a single block.
